Images</span></div><figcaption class="ssrcss-179o3th-StyledFigureCaption ehbdhz00"><span class="visually-hidden ssrcss-1f39n02-VisuallyHidden e16en2lz0">Image caption, </span><div spacing="6" class="ssrcss-y7krbn-Stack e1y4nx260"><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">A Russian hacking group known as Fancy Bear is accused of trying to disrupt the US midterm elections</p></div></figcaption></figure></div><div data-component="text-block" class="ssrcss-uf6wea-RichTextComponentWrapper ep2nwvo0"><div class="ssrcss-7uxr49-RichTextContainer e5tfeyi1"><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10"><b class="ssrcss-1xjjfut-BoldText e5tfeyi3">Russian attempts to launch cyber-attacks against US conservative groups have been thwarted, Microsoft says.</b></p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">The software company <a href="https://blogs.microsoft.com/on-the-issues/2018/08/20/we-are-taking-new-steps-against-broadening-threats-to-democracy/" class="ssrcss-f6h2dj-InlineLink e1kn3p7n0">said Russian hackers had tried to steal data<span class="visually-hidden ssrcss-1f39n02-VisuallyHidden e16en2lz0">, <!-- -->external</span></a> from political organisations, including the International Republican Institute and the Hudson Institute think tanks.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">But they had been thwarted when its security staff had won control of six net domains mimicking their websites.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Microsoft said the Fancy Bear hacking group had been behind the attacks.</p></div></div><div data-component="subheadline-block" class="ssrcss-19w8cxh-ComponentWrapper-HeadlineComponentWrapper egtrm1f0"><h2 id="Domain-control" tabindex="-1" class="ssrcss-pbttu9-Heading e10rt3ze0"><span role="text">Domain control</span></h2></div><div data-component="text-block" class="ssrcss-uf6wea-RichTextComponentWrapper ep2nwvo0"><div class="ssrcss-7uxr49-RichTextContainer e5tfeyi1"><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">&quot;We&#x27;re concerned that these and other attempts pose security threats to a broadening array of groups connected with both American political parties in the run-up to the 2018 elections,&quot; Microsoft said in its blog detailing its work.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">The thwarted attack was likely the start of a &quot;spear phishing&quot; campaign, said Microsoft. This would involve tricking people into visiting the mimicked domains allowing the Fancy Bear group to see and steal login information that people use. </p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">As well as the two think-tanks, the domains seized were associated with several Senate offices and services. One domain sought to mimic Microsoft&#x27;s Office 365 online service.</p></div></div><div data-component="text-block" class="ssrcss-uf6wea-RichTextComponentWrapper ep2nwvo0"><div class="ssrcss-7uxr49-RichTextContainer e5tfeyi1"><div class="ssrcss-1le81vw-ListContainer e5tfeyi0"><ul role="list"><li><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10"><a href="/news/uk-politics-45250069" class="ssrcss-f6h2dj-InlineLink e1kn3p7n0">Hunt wants &#x27;malign&#x27; Russia to face action</a></p></li><li><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10"><a href="/news/technology-45208776" class="ssrcss-f6h2dj-InlineLink e1kn3p7n0">Trump relaxes rules around cyber-attacks</a></p></li><li><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10"><a href="/news/world-us-canada-45047138" class="ssrcss-f6h2dj-InlineLink e1kn3p7n0">US accuses Russia of &#x27;pervasive&#x27; meddling</a></p></li></ul></div></div></div><div data-component="text-block" class="ssrcss-uf6wea-RichTextComponentWrapper ep2nwvo0"><div class="ssrcss-7uxr49-RichTextContainer e5tfeyi1"><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Russia has denied Microsoft&#x27;s allegations that it targeted the right-wing think-tanks. </p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">President Vladimir Putin&#x27;s spokesman Dmitry Peskov said Moscow was &quot;unaware&quot; of any attempted interference by Russia-linked hackers in the US mid-term elections.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">&quot;[Our] reaction is traditional,&quot; he told the Interfax news agency. &quot;We are unaware what kind of hackers they refer to, we do not know what this interference entails.&quot; </p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">BBC Monitoring reported him as adding: &quot;We do not understand whom exactly it concerns, what the evidence is and what such conclusions are based on. We have no such information.&quot;</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">He said: &quot;We hear confirmation from America that there was no meddling in the election.&quot;</p></div></div><div data-component="subheadline-block" class="ssrcss-19w8cxh-ComponentWrapper-HeadlineComponentWrapper egtrm1f0"><h2 id="Spying-charges" tabindex="-1" class="ssrcss-pbttu9-Heading e10rt3ze0"><span role="text">Spying charges</span></h2></div><div data-component="text-block" class="ssrcss-uf6wea-RichTextComponentWrapper ep2nwvo0"><div class="ssrcss-7uxr49-RichTextContainer e5tfeyi1"><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">The <a href="https://www.nytimes.com/2018/08/21/us/politics/russia-cyber-hack.html" class="ssrcss-f6h2dj-InlineLink e1kn3p7n0">New York Times suggested<span class="visually-hidden ssrcss-1f39n02-VisuallyHidden e16en2lz0">, <!-- -->external</span></a> that the two think tanks were targeted because they were former supporters of President Trump but were now foes who had called for more sanctions to be imposed on Russia.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">The International Republican Institute&#x27;s directors include Senator John McCain and General HR McMaster who was replaced earlier this year as the White House national security adviser.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">IRI president Daniel Twining told the Times that the attacks were consistent with the &quot;campaign of meddling&quot; the Kremlin is known to have indulged in.</p></div></div><div data-component="image-block" class="ssrcss-1qlkdz0-ComponentWrapper-FullWidthWrapper ep2nwvo1"><figure class="ssrcss-1vfya96-StyledFigure e34k3c22"><div </span>Crowdstrike</span></div><figcaption class="ssrcss-179o3th-StyledFigureCaption ehbdhz00"><span class="visually-hidden ssrcss-1f39n02-VisuallyHidden e16en2lz0">Image caption, </span><div spacing="6" class="ssrcss-y7krbn-Stack e1y4nx260"><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Some of Fancy Bear&#x27;s activities had previously been identified by the cyber-security company Crowdstrike</p></div></figcaption></figure></div><div data-component="text-block" class="ssrcss-uf6wea-RichTextComponentWrapper ep2nwvo0"><div class="ssrcss-7uxr49-RichTextContainer e5tfeyi1"><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">In its blog, Microsoft president Brad Smith said it had grabbed dodgy domains 12 times in two years to shut down 84 websites associated with Fancy Bear.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">It said that, so far, it had no evidence that the domains had been used in any attacks. The domains could have been set up to help a future planned assault.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Microsoft added that the attack activity seen around the domains &quot;mirrors&quot; what it saw in 2016 in the US and during the 2017 election in France. </p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Microsoft&#x27;s action comes soon after the US charged 12 Russian intelligence officers with hacking computer networks used by Hillary Clinton and the Democratic Party.</p></div></div><div data-component="links-block"
